### Human (05:10:41)

Hi o3

At the next prompt, I am going to provide you with 20 entries from a spreadsheet describing digital resources for archaeology.

We need to improve the data in the following ways:

1. improve its description to a 50-100 word description
2. decide if the following tool definition applies 

<definition>

For our project, a software tool is any discrete piece of software—be it a program, script, or web application—that is developed or substantially modified by researchers to perform specific, research-oriented computational tasks. These tasks must involve active data processing, such as analysis, simulation, visualization, modeling, or automation, where input data is dynamically created, documented, transformed, or interpreted to generate meaningful results. In contrast, products whose primary function is to simply display, store, or promote static datasets—without offering mechanisms for active computational engagement—are excluded. 

In essence, a valid software tool for our purposes is one that not only **supports research in archaeology or historical sciences** but does so by actively collecting and/or processing data rather than merely serving as a generic data repository or static interface.

</definition>

If the resource does meet this definition, please: 

1. Add a new column named 'Tool' to the spreadsheet if it does not already exist.
2. Place the tag 'archhist-software-tool' in that 'Tool' Column to indicate that the resource met our definition of a tool. 

Please ONLY write the 'archhist-software-tool' tag to the new 'Tool' Column, DO NOT place it in any other column.

Please output the updated CSV as a fenced code block. 

Do you understand these instructions?

<definition>

For our project, a software tool is any discrete piece of software—be it a program, script, or web application—that is developed or substantially modified by researchers to perform specific, research-oriented computational tasks. These tasks must involve active data processing, such as analysis, simulation, visualization, modeling, or automation, where input data is dynamically created, documented, transformed, or interpreted to generate meaningful results. In contrast, products whose primary function is to simply display, store, or promote static datasets—without offering mechanisms for active computational engagement—are excluded. 

In essence, a valid software tool for our purposes is one that not only **supports research in archaeology or historical sciences** but does so by actively collecting and/or processing data rather than merely serving as a generic data repository or static interface.

</definition>

If the resource does meet this definition, please: 

1. Add a new column named 'archhist-software-tool' to the spreadsheet if it does not already exist.

The "gamma" package also qualifies as a research tool, given its function in estimating dose rates for luminescence dating, qualifying it for "yes."

Let’s move forward!

**Summarizing tool descriptions and classifications**

For "CloudCal," this is a tool designed for calibration of XRF devices, automating the process of generating calibration curves, marking it as "yes" for being research-oriented.

item_name,description,Improved description,archist-software-tool
neotoma,"Programmatic R interface to the Neotoma Paleoecological Database","neotoma is an R package that serves as a programmatic interface to the Neotoma Paleoecological Database. It enables researchers to query, retrieve, and analyze paleoecological data directly within R. By automating data access and integration, neotoma transforms raw environmental datasets into dynamic visualizations and statistical models, thereby supporting advanced quantitative analyses in paleoclimate and archaeological research.",yes
c14bazAAR,"R package to query different openly accessible radiocarbon date databases, allowing for basic data cleaning, calibration and merging","c14bazAAR is an R package designed for querying multiple radiocarbon date databases. It automates the retrieval, cleaning, calibration, and merging of radiocarbon dating records. By integrating these functions into a cohesive toolkit, c14bazAAR enables researchers to dynamically process chronological data and streamline radiocarbon analysis, enhancing the efficiency and reproducibility of chronological modeling in archaeological studies.",yes
paleofire,"An R package to analyse sedimentary charcoal records from the Global Charcoal Database to reconstruct past biomass burning","paleofire is an R package developed to analyze sedimentary charcoal records from the Global Charcoal Database. It actively processes charcoal count and distribution data to reconstruct historical biomass burning patterns and infer changes in fire regimes over time. Through integrated statistical analyses and visualizations, paleofire converts raw sediment data into informative models, supporting research in paleoclimate modeling and archaeological environmental studies.",yes
archaeology-data-service,"An app to collect data on archaeological objects.","archaeology-data-service is a mobile application designed for the collection of archaeological object data in the field. It provides a digital interface for recording artifact information and metadata during excavations. However, its functionality focuses primarily on data collection and storage rather than on active computational processing, analysis, or transformation of data.",no
munsell-plot.R,"Make a stratigraphic-style plot-schematic of sediment colour using munsell values","munsell-plot.R is an R script that generates stratigraphic-style plots by mapping sediment colors based on Munsell values. It actively processes input data representing sediment color attributes and produces visual plots that assist in interpreting stratigraphic sequences. This automated visualization aids researchers in understanding depositional environments and sedimentary variations in archaeological and geological contexts.",yes
Ceramic-Frequency-Date-Plot,"This R script produces a exploratory visual for assessing site date ranges originally suggested to me by Wesley Bernardini Redlands University","Ceramic-Frequency-Date-Plot is an R script that creates exploratory visualizations for assessing site date ranges based on ceramic frequency data. It processes temporal and quantitative ceramic data to generate plots that reveal chronological trends and potential dating ranges. By automating this visualization process, the script assists researchers in identifying temporal patterns and refining chronological interpretations in ceramic analysis.",yes
Ford-Diagram,"This R Function creates a simple Ford diagram for archaeological seriation with error bars determined based on sample size were count data are given","Ford-Diagram is an R function that generates Ford diagrams for archaeological seriation. It processes count data to produce visual representations of artifact frequency distributions over time, complete with error bars based on sample size. This dynamic tool assists researchers in interpreting seriation results and assessing chronological sequences in archaeological datasets.",yes
osteoGIS,"Plot data on skeletal templates quickly","osteoGIS is an R package that enables rapid plotting of skeletal data onto standardized templates. It actively processes osteological measurements to overlay data on skeletal diagrams, facilitating quick visualization of spatial patterns and variations. This tool streamlines bioarchaeological analysis by providing an accessible method for visualizing skeletal data.",yes
munsell,"Provides easy access to, and manipulation of, the Munsell colours","munsell is an R package offering functions for accessing and manipulating Munsell color data. It allows conversion, visualization, and comparison of color values, supporting analyses in fields such as sediment color interpretation and art conservation. By enabling dynamic color processing and transformation, munsell assists researchers in enhancing the visual representation of data.",yes
khroma,"Colour Schemes for Archaeological Data Visualization","khroma is an R package that provides curated color schemes for archaeological data visualization. It actively generates and manipulates color palettes to enhance the clarity and interpretability of visualizations. By integrating color theory with data presentation, khroma helps researchers create compelling and informative plots for archaeological and historical datasets.",yes
rekrei,"Platform for crowdsourcing the digital recreation of lost heritage","rekrei is a standalone software platform that leverages crowdsourcing to digitally reconstruct lost heritage. It actively processes user-submitted 3D models, images, and annotations to generate detailed digital recreations of archaeological sites and artifacts. By combining collaborative inputs with advanced rendering techniques, rekrei facilitates dynamic restoration and visualization of heritage, supporting both research and public engagement.",yes
archaeological-object-sharing,"An online space for sharing data, 3d models, etc about archaeological objects to enable the comparison of these objects.","archaeological-object-sharing is a standalone platform designed for sharing data and 3D models of archaeological objects. Its primary function is to provide a collaborative online repository for artifact information rather than to process data actively. As such, it serves as a static interface for data sharing and does not meet the criteria for an active research-oriented computational tool.",no
open-context-py,"This project represents the current evolution of Open Context. It's intended to be an easier to maintain code-base, and to make the data published by Open Context easier to maintain.","open-context-py is a software project that represents the evolution of the Open Context platform, aimed at simplifying data maintenance and accessibility. While it improves the management and dissemination of archaeological data, its core functionality focuses on data organization rather than on dynamic computational processing or analysis.",no
paleocore,"Towards a data standard for paleoanthropology.","paleocore is a standalone software tool developed to establish data standards for paleoanthropology. It provides a framework for organizing and sharing paleoanthropological data, promoting consistency across datasets. However, its main function is centered on data formatting and standardization rather than on active data processing, limiting its classification as a dynamic analytical tool.",no
poseidon-framework,"Poseidon is a framework that seeks to provide standardized ways to store and share archaeogenetic, and perhaps more broadly, molecular archaeological datasets.","poseidon-framework is a software framework designed to standardize the storage and sharing of archaeogenetic and molecular archaeological data. It offers structured schemas to facilitate data interoperability. Although it improves data organization and exchange, its focus on standardization and storage means it does not perform active computational processing or analysis.",no
totalopenstation,"Total Open Station downloads and exports survey data from your total station.","totalopenstation is a standalone software tool that downloads and exports survey data directly from total station devices. It actively processes raw measurement data and converts it into standardized formats for subsequent mapping and analysis, thereby streamlining field data management in archaeological surveys.",yes
totalstation-tools,"Tools to use and manipulate total station data","totalstation-tools is a Python package that provides a suite of functions for processing and manipulating data from total station surveying instruments. It actively converts and analyzes spatial measurements, facilitating the transformation and visualization of survey data for archaeological mapping and geospatial analysis.",yes
LA_ICP_MS-Routines_FMNH,"Routines to read and analyze LA-ICP-MS data from the Field Museum's Elemental Analysis Facility","LA_ICP_MS-Routines_FMNH is an R package that reads, processes, and analyzes LA-ICP-MS data from the Field Museum's Elemental Analysis Facility. It actively processes geochemical data to produce quantitative outputs and visualizations, aiding in the interpretation of elemental compositions in archaeological materials.",yes
archaeology_on_wikipedia.R,"How does wikipedia see archaeology?","archaeology_on_wikipedia.R is an R script that analyzes how Wikipedia portrays archaeology by extracting and processing article data. It actively retrieves, organizes, and visualizes Wikipedia content to provide insights into public perceptions of archaeological topics, supporting digital humanities research through dynamic text analysis.",yes
tweet-edits-to-archaeology-articles.R,"Using R with wikipedia for various things","tweet-edits-to-archaeology-articles.R is an R script that integrates Twitter and Wikipedia data to examine edits and interactions related to archaeology articles. It actively processes social media and encyclopedic data to generate analyses of public engagement and editorial trends, facilitating digital humanities research.",yes
dayofarchaeology,"A Distant Reading of the Day of Archaeology","dayofarchaeology is an R-based digital humanities project that performs a distant reading of the Day of Archaeology. It actively processes large-scale text and social media data to analyze themes, trends, and public engagement with archaeological content, bridging data science and public archaeology.",yes

It actively processes spatial data to create multiple map visualizations from varying perspectives, enabling researchers to analyze the interplay between environmental factors and archaeological site distribution.",yes

It actively processes geospatial data to visualize areas at risk, integrating archaeological site information with disaster management strategies to assess spatial vulnerabilities.",yes

### Tool (06:13:19)

**Evaluating tool criteria**

I need to produce output in CSV format with columns: 'item_name', 'description', 'Improved description', and 'archist-software-tool'. The 'archist-software-tool' column should be marked "yes" if the resource meets the tool definition (something directly used for research-oriented tasks like analysis). Otherwise, it’ll be "no". 

I'll look over the list of entries and decide which tools qualify as software tools under this definition. The key is confirming whether they actively process data or just manage it. Let's get to work!

**Analyzing "cca" as a tool**

Looking at "Colossal Cave Adventure digital palaeography and epigraphy project," I’m weighing if it fits the criteria for an active research tool. It started as a text-based game, and while the project re-contextualizes it for archaeology, it still mainly seems to be a game. The description talks about analyzing texts, but it's not clear that it's performing active computational tasks for research. So, I'll mark this as "no" for the tool category.

For the improved description: "cca repurposes the Colossal Cave Adventure game to explore digital palaeography and epigraphy, bridging interactive gameplay with analysis of ancient inscriptions."

**Improving descriptions for research tools**

For "cca", it's primarily focused on digital storytelling rather than active computational tasks for research, so I marked it "no". I crafted this improved description: "cca adapts the classic game to explore palaeography and epigraphy, mixing interactive narrative with the study of ancient texts. Though insightful, its aim is more entertainment than rigorous data processing for research."

For "archaeology-grand-challenges.r", that's more of a conceptual, static document, so it doesn't fit as a research tool. Hence, it's marked "no" too. The description stresses its value for inspiration rather than computation.

**Improving descriptions for active research tools**

For "soiltexture," it processes soil data into visual diagrams like texture triangles, so I marked it "yes" for being a research tool. The improved description highlights its ability to classify and transform soil texture data into useful visual representations for researchers.

For "sparch," it's an R package enhancing spatial data operations. It processes data actively—marking it as a research tool—making it helpful for geospatial analysis in archaeology. Here's the description emphasizing its utility in spatial data research with efficient processing.

**Improving descriptions for tools**

For "demjanp," which is designed to calculate radiocarbon dating resolution, it's a Python tool that actively processes radiocarbon data using calibration and statistical algorithms. The improved description explains how it refines chronological models, improving the precision of radiocarbon dating estimates in archaeological research.

For "arkhe," an R package for data cleaning, it’s used to process rectangular datasets by detecting errors and normalizing data. The description focuses on how it enhances reliability in archaeological and quantitative research workflows, streamlining data cleaning for further analysis. Both are valuable computational tools!

<definition>

For our project, a software tool is any discrete piece of software—be it a program, script, or web application—that is developed or substantially modified by researchers to perform specific, research-oriented computational tasks. These tasks must involve active data processing, such as analysis, simulation, visualization, modeling, or automation, where input data is dynamically created, documented, transformed, or interpreted to generate meaningful results. In contrast, products whose primary function is to simply display, store, or promote static datasets—without offering mechanisms for active computational engagement—are excluded. 

In essence, a valid software tool for our purposes is one that not only **supports research in archaeology or historical sciences** but does so by actively collecting and/or processing data rather than merely serving as a generic data repository or static interface.

</definition>

If the resource does meet this definition, please: 

1. Add a new column named 'archhist-software-tool' to the spreadsheet if it does not already exist.

Some tools, like HumanOS, might fall short because they mainly collect or store data rather than process it. Time to keep working through the list!

**Evaluating plugin functionality**

The Piwigo plugin for viewing 3D models seems focused on display, not data processing. It's described as a tool for visualizing 3D models using the 3DHOP framework. Since it enhances how the data is presented rather than analyzing or processing the data itself, it’s likely a "no" in terms of meeting the active data processing criteria. Despite its useful visualization capabilities, it doesn’t transform or interpret data, which is essential for a tool to meet the "active processing" definition. So, I’d say it's not classified as a software tool here.

**Processing data management tools**

The `iDAI.field` system integrates GIS, photo management, and database management into a comprehensive tool for field research documentation. While it supports archaeological data collection and storage, it mainly focuses on organizing and managing data rather than actively processing it. This means that it doesn’t quite fit the "research-oriented computational tool" definition. It's more about data management and display, rather than dynamically analyzing or processing data to generate results, so it doesn't meet the active processing criteria. Thus, it would be classified as "no."

### Human (06:45:17)

Hi o3

At the next prompt, I am going to provide you with entries from a spreadsheet describing digital resources for archaeology.

We need to improve the data in the following ways:

1. improve its description to a 50-100 word description
2. decide if the following tool definition applies 

<definition>

For our project, a software tool is any discrete piece of software—be it a program, script, or web application—that is developed or substantially modified by researchers to perform specific, research-oriented computational tasks. These tasks must involve active data processing, such as analysis, simulation, visualization, modeling, or automation, where input data is dynamically created, documented, transformed, or interpreted to generate meaningful results. In contrast, products whose primary function is to simply display, store, or promote static datasets—without offering mechanisms for active computational engagement—are excluded. 

In essence, a valid software tool for our purposes is one that not only **supports research in archaeology or historical sciences** but does so by actively collecting and/or processing data rather than merely serving as a generic data repository or static interface.

</definition>

If the resource does meet this definition, please: 

1. Add a new column named 'archhist-software-tool' to the spreadsheet if it does not already exist.
2. Place a 'yes' or a 'no' in that column to indicate whether or not the resource meets our definition of a tool. 

Output:

Please output the following columns: 'item_name' (unchanged from original), 'description' (with the original description), 'Improved description' (with your improved description), and 'archist-software-tool' as a CSV in a fenced code block. 

Do you understand these instructions?

Hi o3

At the next prompt, I am going to provide you with entries from a spreadsheet describing digital resources for archaeology.

We need to improve the data in the following ways:

1. improve its description to a 50-100 word description
2. decide if the following tool definition applies 

<definition>

For our project, a software tool is any discrete piece of software—be it a program, script, or web application—that is developed or substantially modified by researchers to perform specific, research-oriented computational tasks. These tasks must involve active data processing, such as analysis, simulation, visualization, modeling, or automation, where input data is dynamically created, documented, transformed, or interpreted to generate meaningful results. In contrast, products whose primary function is to simply display, store, or promote static datasets—without offering mechanisms for active computational engagement—are excluded. 

In essence, a valid software tool for our purposes is one that not only **supports research in archaeology or historical sciences** but does so by actively collecting and/or processing data rather than merely serving as a generic data repository or static interface.

</definition>

If the resource does meet this definition, please: 

1. Add a new column named 'archhist-software-tool' to the spreadsheet if it does not already exist.
2. Place a 'yes' or a 'no' in that column to indicate whether or not the resource meets our definition of a tool. 

Output:

Please output the following columns: 'item_name' (unchanged from original), 'description' (with the original description), 'Improved description' (with your improved description), and 'archist-software-tool' as a CSV in a fenced code block. 

Do you understand these instructions?
